Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor that arises from the odontogenic epithelium (tooth-forming tissue) and can cause jaw swelling and pain, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of odontogenic cyst that forms around the crown of an unerupted tooth and can cause jaw swelling and pain, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more of the bones surrounding the eye and can cause double vision, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the jaw joints become fused and can cause difficulty opening the mouth, but it is known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor that arises from the odontogenic epithelium (tooth-forming tissue) and can cause jaw swelling and pain, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of odontogenic cyst that forms from the accumulation of fluid between the reduced enamel epithelium and the tooth crown. It can cause swelling and displacement of teeth, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more of the bones surrounding the eye and can cause double vision, pain, and swelling around the eye, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the temporomandibular joint (TMJ) is fused, preventing normal jaw movement. This can cause difficulty opening the mouth, pain, and difficulty eating, and it is known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.

Question: Gum pads are divided into following segments:
Choices:
  A: 3 in each quadrant
  B: 2 in each jaw
  C: 5 in each quadrant
  D: 2 in each quadrant
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Gum pads are also known as interdental papilla.
  They are the triangular shaped gum tissue that fills the space between two teeth.
  The number of gum pads varies depending on the number of teeth in each quadrant of the mouth.
  A: 3 gum pads in each quadrant would mean a total of 12 gum pads in the mouth, which is not accurate.
  B: 2 gum pads in each jaw would mean a total of 4 gum pads in the mouth, which is not accurate.
  C: 5 gum pads in each quadrant would mean a total of 20 gum pads in the mouth, which is not accurate.
  D: 2 gum pads in each quadrant would mean a total of 8 gum pads in the mouth, which is accurate.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that requires immediate treatment.
  HDL, LDL, and TG are types of cholesterol.
  High levels of LDL and TG and low levels of HDL are risk factors for cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are a class of drugs that lower cholesterol levels.
  Fenofibrate is a fibrate drug that lowers triglyceride levels.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  The patient has high levels of TG and low levels of HDL, which are both risk factors for cardiovascular disease. Therefore, a combination of a statin and a fibrate drug is preferred for this patient. Rosuvastatin and fenofibrate are both effective in lowering cholesterol levels, and their combination has been shown to reduce the risk of cardiovascular events. Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and may increase the risk of side effects, and rosuvastatin 10 mg alone may not be sufficient to lower TG levels. Therefore, the preferred option is Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that occurs when blood flow to the heart muscle is blocked.
  HDL is the "good" cholesterol, while LDL is the "bad" cholesterol.
  High levels of triglycerides (TG) are associated with an increased risk of heart disease.
  Statins are a class of drugs that lower cholesterol levels in the blood.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that lowers triglyceride levels and raises HDL cholesterol levels.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  The patient has a high level of triglycerides and low level of HDL cholesterol, which puts him at risk for cardiovascular disease. The preferred treatment for this patient would be a combination of a statin and a fibrate, such as Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate. This combination has been shown to reduce the risk of cardiovascular events in patients with high triglycerides and low HDL cholesterol levels. Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and may not be necessary for this patient. Rosuvastatin 10 mg alone may not be enough to lower the triglyceride levels. Fenofibrate alone may raise the risk of adverse effects.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that occurs when blood flow to the heart muscle is blocked.
  HDL is the "good" cholesterol that helps remove LDL from the arteries.
  LDL is the "bad" cholesterol that can build up in the arteries and cause blockages.
  TG (triglycerides) are a type of fat found in the blood that can also contribute to the development of heart disease.
  Statins are a class of drugs that can lower LDL cholesterol levels.
  Fenofibrate is a drug that can lower TG levels and increase HDL levels.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  The patient has a high TG level and low HDL level, which puts them at risk for cardiovascular disease. The preferred treatment for this patient would be a combination of a statin (such as Rosuvastatin) and a fibrate (such as Fenofibrate) to lower both LDL and TG levels and increase HDL levels. Therefore, the best option is A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.

Statins are the first-line therapy for reducing LDL cholesterol levels, while fibrates are used to lower triglyceride levels and increase HDL levels. Combination therapy with a statin and a fibrate may be considered in patients with high triglyceride levels and low HDL levels.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity located in the midline of the brain, between the two thalami.
  A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic nerve to the brain, and it is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) is a cranial nerve that controls the movement of the eye, and it is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a stalk-like structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus, and it is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain, and they are not located on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity located in the midline of the brain, between the two thalami.
  A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic nerve to the brain and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) is a cranial nerve that controls the movement of certain eye muscles and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures that are part of the limbic system and are located on the posterior wall of the third ventricle, not on the floor.

Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  T4 is a thyroid hormone that is important for growth and development.
  TSH is a hormone that stimulates the thyroid gland to produce T4.
  A: Primary hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone.
  B: A pituitary tumor can cause an increase in TSH secretion, which can lead to an increase in thyroid hormone production.
  C: A TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a type of pituitary tumor that produces excess TSH, leading to an increase in thyroid hormone production.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare condition where the thyroid gland is resistant to the effects of TSH, leading to decreased thyroid hormone production.
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  T4 is a thyroid hormone that is produced by the thyroid gland.
  TSH is a hormone that is produced by the pituitary gland and stimulates the thyroid gland to produce T4.
  A: Primary hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone.
  B: A pituitary tumor is a growth in the pituitary gland that can cause hormonal imbalances.
  C: A TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a type of pituitary tumor that produces excess TSH.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder where the thyroid gland is resistant to the effects of TSH.
  
Analysis:
  The child is short, which suggests a growth hormone deficiency. The low T4 and raised TSH suggest hypothyroidism. The swelling of the pituitary suggests a pituitary tumor. The most likely diagnosis is a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.

Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure that involves the complete removal of the dental pulp, while pulp capping is a procedure that involves the placement of a medicament over an exposed pulp to promote healing and the formation of a dentin bridge.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in a child's mouth and are eventually replaced by permanent teeth.
  A: Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin, which is the hard tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth. Increased odontoblastic activity in young teeth may contribute to the success of pulpectomy and pulp capping.
  B: Blood supply is important for the healing process, but it is not a major factor in the success of pulpectomy and pulp capping.
  C: The volume of pulp in primary teeth is smaller than in permanent teeth, which may make the procedures easier to perform, but it is not a major factor in their success.
  D: Collagen fibers are a major component of the pulp tissue, but their amount is not a major factor in the success of pulpectomy and pulp capping.

Choices:
  A: >50 degree
  B: >90 degree
  C: <50 degree
  D: <90 degree
Response 0:

  C: A>D>B>C

  The auditory pathway can be divided into two main pathways: the primary pathway and the secondary pathway.
  The primary pathway is responsible for processing sound localization and intensity, while the secondary pathway is responsible for processing sound quality and recognition.

Question: A patient sustained A and endotracheal intubation was done. Most likely GCS score of such a patient would be:March 2013 (b, c, d)
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 10
  C: 12
  D: 15
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The Glasgow Coma Scale (GCS) is used to assess the level of consciousness of a patient. It is based on three parameters: eye opening, verbal response, and motor response. The score ranges from 3 to 15, with a score of 3 indicating deep unconsciousness and a score of 15 indicating full consciousness.
  Endotracheal intubation is a procedure in which a tube is inserted through the mouth or nose into the trachea to help a patient breathe.
  A: A GCS score of 8 indicates a severe brain injury and is associated with a comatose state.
  B: A GCS score of 10 indicates a moderate brain injury and is associated with a state of confusion.
  C: A GCS score of 12 indicates a mild brain injury and is associated with a state of disorientation.
  D: A GCS score of 15 indicates full consciousness.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The Glasgow Coma Scale (GCS) is used to assess the level of consciousness of a patient. 
  The GCS score ranges from 3 to 15, with 3 being the worst possible score and 15 being the best possible score.
  A: A GCS score of 8 indicates a severe brain injury and a patient is usually in a coma.
  B: A GCS score of 10 indicates a moderate brain injury and a patient may be confused or disoriented.
  C: A GCS score of 12 indicates a mild brain injury and a patient may have some confusion or disorientation.
  D: A GCS score of 15 indicates that the patient is fully conscious and alert.
  
Action: Answer("B")

Topic: Dental
Question: Which of the following are the predominant connective tissue cells of the periodontal Ligament?
Choices:
  A: Cementoblasts
  B: Fibroblasts
  C: Osteoblasts
  D: Rests of Malassez
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The periodontal ligament is a specialized connective tissue that surrounds and attaches teeth to the alveolar bone.
  A: Cementoblasts are cells that form cementum, a mineralized tissue that covers the root of the tooth.
  B: Fibroblasts are the predominant connective tissue cells of the periodontal ligament.
  C: Osteoblasts are cells that form bone tissue.
  D: Rests of Malassez are remnants of Hertwig's epithelial root sheath that persist in the periodontal ligament after tooth formation.

Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The periodontal ligament is a specialized connective tissue that surrounds and attaches teeth to the alveolar bone.

  C: Osteoblasts are cells that form bone tissue.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root surface of a tooth.
  PDL stands for periodontal ligament, which is a group of fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  Cementum is a layer of hard tissue that covers the root of a tooth.
  Dentin is a hard tissue that makes up the bulk of a tooth.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the body.
  
Answer: 
  A lateral sliding flap is used to access the root surface of a tooth. If the roots have been denuded for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibers have been lost. Therefore, the flap will show PDL fibers attached to cementum. 
  Choice A is the best answer. 
  B, C, and D are not correct.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root surface of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  A: PDL (periodontal ligament) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum. If the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is unlikely that PDL fibres will be attached to the cementum.
  B: PDL fibres are attached to dentin, but if the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is unlikely that PDL fibres will be attached to the dentin.
  C: Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the tooth. If the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is likely that epithelium will be adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.
  D: Co adaptation refers to the ability of the PDL fibres to adapt to changes in the tooth position. If the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is unlikely that there will be remaining fibres to co adapt to.
Action: Answer("C")

  Dentin is a hard, mineralized tissue that makes up the bulk of a tooth.

Question: Cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy?
Choices:
  A: Amacrine cells
  B: Bipolar cells
  C: Ganglion cells
  D: Rods and cones
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Glaucomatous optic atrophy is a condition that results from damage to the optic nerve, which is responsible for transmitting visual information from the eye to the brain.
  A: Amacrine cells are interneurons in the retina that modulate the activity of other retinal cells, but they are not directly involved in transmitting visual information to the brain.
  B: Bipolar cells are retinal cells that receive input from photoreceptor cells (rods and cones) and transmit signals to ganglion cells, but they are not directly involved in transmitting visual information to the brain.
  C: Ganglion cells are the retinal cells that transmit visual information to the brain via the optic nerve. They are the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
  D: Rods and cones are photoreceptor cells in the retina that are responsible for detecting light and initiating the visual process, but they are not directly involved in transmitting visual information to the brain.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The Bishop score is used to assess the readiness of the cervix for induction of labor.
  The score is based on five components: cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station.
  The maximum score is 13.
  A score of 8 or higher indicates that the cervix is favorable for induction.
  
In this case:
  Cervical dilation = 1 cm
  Cervical effacement = 30%
  Cervical consistency = Soft
  Cervical position = Posterior
  Fetal station = -1
  
Action: Answer("B")  
The modified Bishop score for this lady is 3.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The Bishop score is used to assess the cervical readiness for induction of labor. It is based on five components: cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station. Each component is scored from 0 to 2, and the scores are added up to give a total score ranging from 0 to 13. A score of 8 or higher is considered favorable for induction of labor.
  In this case, the patient is a primigravida at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation with a cervix that is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior.

Analysis:
  The Bishop score components for this patient are:
  - Cervical dilation: 1 cm (score 0)
  - Cervical effacement: 30% (score 0)
  - Cervical consistency: soft (score 2)
  - Cervical position: posterior (score 0)
  - Fetal station: -1 (score 1)
  The total Bishop score is 0 + 0 + 2 + 0 + 1 = 3.

  B: Lecithin-cephalin ratio
  C: Phosphatidyl choline
  D: Phosphatidyl glycerol

Knowledge:
  In diabetic mothers, fetal lung maturity is delayed, and the risk of respiratory distress syndrome (RDS) is increased in neonates.

  C: Long half-life permits altemate day dosing

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: A female come to gynaeoPD for preconceptual counseling, with history of two second trimester aboions. What is the next investigation you will advice
Choices:
  A: TVS
  B: hysteroscopy
  C: Endometrial biopsy
  D: chromosomal abnormalities
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Preconceptual counseling is a type of medical consultation that aims to prepare a woman for pregnancy.
  Second trimester abortions are those that occur between 13 and 28 weeks of pregnancy.
  A: Transvaginal ultrasound (TVS) is a type of imaging test that uses sound waves to create pictures of the inside of the pelvic area.
  B: Hysteroscopy is a procedure that allows a doctor to look inside the uterus in order to diagnose and treat problems.
  C: Endometrial biopsy is a procedure that involves taking a small sample of tissue from the lining of the uterus in order to diagnose certain conditions.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities are genetic disorders that can cause problems with growth, development, and overall health.
  
Answer: B) hysteroscopy. 
Explanation: In this case, the patient has a history of two second trimester abortions, which could be due to uterine abnormalities. Hysteroscopy is a procedure that allows a doctor to look inside the uterus and diagnose any structural abnormalities that may be contributing to the patient's history of miscarriages. Therefore, hysteroscopy is the most appropriate investigation to advise in this situation.

  B: Type 2 refers to two canals that join into one canal before exiting at the apex.

Choices:

  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  A: Occlusal balancing refers to the adjustment of the contact between the teeth during biting and chewing. It is not related to looseness of RPD.
  B: Passive clasp on abutment refers to a clasp that does not engage the abutment tooth when the RPD is seated. It may cause the RPD to be loose.
  C: Thin flange refers to the part of the RPD that extends into the vestibule. If it is too thin, it may cause the RPD to be loose.
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth refers to the lack of coverage of the RPD on the posterior teeth. It may cause the RPD to be loose.
Action: Answer("B")

Knowledge:

  Extraction is not usually the first line of treatment for caries in primary teeth.

  Restoration involves removing the decayed part of the tooth and filling it with a restorative material.

Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Acromegaly is a hormonal disorder that results from excessive growth hormone (GH) production by the pituitary gland.
  A: A large tongue is a feature of macroglossia, which may be seen in some conditions such as Down syndrome, hypothyroidism, and amyloidosis, but it is not a feature of acromegaly.
  B: Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, which may be seen in some genetic syndromes such as Pierre Robin syndrome, but it is not a feature of acromegaly.
  C: Hypoglycemia is a condition where the blood glucose level is abnormally low, which may be seen in some conditions such as insulinoma, but it is not a feature of acromegaly.
  D: Crowded teeth may be seen in some conditions such as malocclusion, but it is not a feature of acromegaly.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: A large tongue is a feature of macroglossia, which can be seen in conditions such as Down syndrome, hypothyroidism, and amyloidosis.
  B: Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, which can be seen in Pierre Robin syndrome, Treacher Collins syndrome, and some cases of cleft palate.
  C: Hypoglycemia is a condition where the blood sugar level is abnormally low, which can be seen in insulinoma, Addison's disease, and some cases of liver disease.
  D: Crowded teeth is a common feature of malocclusion, which can be seen in many conditions that affect the development of the teeth and jaws.

Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development has four stages: Sensorimotor, Pre-operational, Concrete operations, and Formal operations.
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen, heard, or touched.
  Object permanence is first developed in the Sensorimotor stage.
  In the Pre-operational stage, children develop symbolic thinking and language, but they do not yet have a full understanding of object permanence.
  In the Concrete operations stage, children develop logical thinking and can understand conservation, but they have already developed object permanence in the previous stage.
  In the Formal operations stage, individuals develop abstract thinking and can reason about hypothetical situations.

  Proteinuria is the presence of excess proteins in the urine.
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Severe preeclampsia is a more severe form of preeclampsia that can lead to serious complications for both the mother and the baby.
  Proteinuria is one of the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
Action: Answer("D")  
Explanation: 
  The level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is 3000 mg or more in a 24-hour urine collection.

  The skin is the outermost layer of the body, while the mucosa is a moist tissue layer that lines various cavities and organs in the body.

  B: Keratinized mucosa is found in areas of the body that are subject to high levels of friction and wear, such as the palms of the hands and the soles of the feet. The mucosa of the cheek is non-keratinized.
  C: Rete pegs are finger-like projections of the epithelium that extend into the underlying connective tissue. They are found in the mucosa of the cheek, but not in the skin.
  D: The lamina propria is a layer of loose connective tissue that underlies the epithelium. It is thicker in the mucosa of the cheek than in the skin.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Orthopaedics
Question: A 9 year old boy presenting with lytic lesion on midshaft tibia. On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Xray is as shown below. What is the likely diagnosis?
Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis is a rare disorder characterized by the proliferation of Langerhans cells, abnormal cells deriving from bone marrow and capable of migrating from skin to lymph nodes.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign tumor of bone characterized by the presence of multinucleated giant cells.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare, benign bone tumor that arises from cartilage cells.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that usually develops in the long bones of the body, such as the femur and tibia.
  Lytic lesion on midshaft tibia with grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation is a characteristic of osteoid osteoma.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis is a rare disorder characterized by the proliferation of Langerhans cells.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign tumor of the bone characterized by the presence of multinucleated giant cells.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare, benign bone tumor that arises from cartilage cells.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that typically occurs in children and young adults and is characterized by the presence of a nidus of osteoid tissue.
  Lytic lesion on midshaft tibia with grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation is suggestive of a diagnosis of osteoblastoma or osteosarcoma.

  B: Prostaglandin E2
  C: Histamine
  D: Serotonin

  A: Thromboxane A2 causes vasoconstriction, which increases blood pressure.
  B: Prostaglandin E2 causes vasodilation, which decreases blood pressure.
  C: Histamine causes vasodilation, which increases blood flow and capillary permeability.
  D: Serotonin causes vasoconstriction, which increases blood pressure.

  C: Histamine is a vasodilator, which means it causes widening of blood vessels.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 79 of 100 ###
Topic: Pediatrics
Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is 
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  1. Jaundice is a yellowish discoloration of the skin and mucous membranes due to an increase in bilirubin levels in the blood.
